(Paper)
<span class="italic"><a title="Link to journal home page" href="https://doi.org/10.1039/2046-2069/2011">RSC Adv.</a></span>, 2023, <strong>13</strong>, 16749-16757</div><h1 id="sect209"><span class="title_heading">Revealing the effect of Nb or V doping on anode performance in Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> for sodium-ion batteries: a first-principles study<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a></span></h1><p class="header_text">
<span class="bold">Suk-Gyong Hwang</span>, 
<span class="bold">Chung-Hyok Kim</span>, 
<span class="bold">Song-Hyok Choe</span>, 
<span class="bold">Kum-Chol Ri</span><span class="bold"> and </span>
<span class="bold">Chol-Jun Yu</span><span class="orcid"><a target="_blank" title="Select to open ORCID record for Chol-Jun&nbsp;Yu (orcid.org/0000-0001-9523-4325) in a new window" id="connect-orcid-link" href="http://orcid.org/0000-0001-9523-4325"><img id="orcid-id-logo" src="/content/NewImages/orcid_16x16.png" alt="ORCID logo"></a></span>*
<br><span class="italic">Computational Materials Design, Faculty of Materials Science, Kim Il Sung University, PO Box 76, Pyongyang, Democratic Peoples Republic of Korea. E-mail: <a href="mailto:cj.yu@ryongnamsan.edu.kp">cj.yu@ryongnamsan.edu.kp</a></span>
</p><div id="art-admin"><span class="italic bold">Received 
17th March 2023
</span><span class="bold italic">, Accepted 11th May 2023</span></div><p class="bold italic">First published on 5th June 2023</p><hr><div class="abstract"><h2>Abstract</h2><p>Sodium titanate Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (NTO) has superior electrochemical properties as an anode material in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), and Nb or V doping is suggested to enhance the electrode performance. In this work, we carry out systematic first-principles calculations of the structural, electronic and electrochemical properties of NTO and Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>2.75</sub></small>M<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (M = Nb, V), using supercells to reveal the effect of Nb or V NTO-doping on its anode performance. It is found that Nb doping gives rise to the expansion of cell volume but V doping induces the shrinkage of cell volume due to the larger and smaller ionic radius of the Nb and V ions, respectively, compared to that of the Ti ion. We perform structural optimization of the intermediate phases of Na<small><sub>2+<span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>M<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> with increasing Na content <span class="italic">x</span> from 0 to 2, revealing that the overall relative volume expansion rate is slightly increased by Nb and V doping but remains lower than 3%. Our calculations demonstrate that the electrode potential of NTO is slightly raised and the specific capacity is reduced, but the electronic and ionic conductivities are improved by Nb or V doping. With the revealed understanding and mechanisms, our work will contribute to the search for advanced electrode materials for SIBs.</p></div><hr>
<h2 id="sect274"><span class="a_heading">1 Introduction</span></h2>
<span>Recently, increasing attention has been paid to developing and utilizing renewable and clean energy sources such as solar energy, wind power and tidal power, to mitigate the serious challenges of global warming and the energy crisis. For progress, an indispensable prerequisite is to develop large-scale electrochemical energy storage (EES) systems that are low cost, high performance and have a long lifetime.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit1"><sup><span class="sup_ref">1</span></sup></a> Among the various EES devices, lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) are highly promising due to their high energy density and long-term cycling life, and are widely used for portable electronic appliances and electric vehicles. However, the limited reserves of Li resources have caused a rapid increase in cost, making them unsuitable for large-scale EES systems.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit2"><sup><span class="sup_ref">2,3</span></sup></a> In this context, there is renewed interest in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) as a promising alternative to LIBs due to the global abundance and low cost of Na resources.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit4"><sup><span class="sup_ref">46</span></sup></a> To realize commercially viable SIBs, however, suitable electrode materials need be developed.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit7"><sup><span class="sup_ref">7,8</span></sup></a> Although graphite is a typical intercalation-type anode material for LIBs, it is not suitable for SIBs because of the larger radius of the Na ion (1.02 ) compared to the Li ion (0.76 ), which has created an intensive search for alternative co-intercalation<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit9"><sup><span class="sup_ref">911</span></sup></a> and hard carbon materials.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit12"><sup><span class="sup_ref">1214</span></sup></a></span>
<p class="otherpara">Sodium titanates with the general chemical formula <span class="italic">n</span>Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<span class="italic">m</span>TiO<small><sub>2</sub></small>, characterized by layered or tunnel structures, have been adopted as promising insertion-type anode materials for SIBs due to their low cost, low electrode potential and non-toxicity.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit15"><sup><span class="sup_ref">1520</span></sup></a> Nanophase titanium dioxide, TiO<small><sub>2</sub></small> (<span class="italic">n</span> = 0), with rutile,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit21"><sup><span class="sup_ref">21</span></sup></a> anatase,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit22"><sup><span class="sup_ref">22</span></sup></a> hollandite<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit23"><sup><span class="sup_ref">23</span></sup></a> and trigonal bipyramid<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit16"><sup><span class="sup_ref">16,24</span></sup></a> structures has shown reversible capacities of 100150 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> due to the Ti<small><sup>3+/4+</sup></small> redox couple. However, these compounds have a relatively high electrode potential of over 0.5 V and lower rate capability compared to hard carbon. The tunnel-structured sodium titanates such as NaTi<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>4</sub></small>,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit25"><sup><span class="sup_ref">25</span></sup></a> Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>4</sub></small>O<small><sub>9</sub></small> (ref. <a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit26">26</a>) and Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>6</sub></small>O<small><sub>13</sub></small> (ref. <a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit27">2730</a>), have also been reported to show reversible sodium insertion/extraction capacities of 45 and 66 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at a high current rate of 2 A g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (30C) with long cycling life (5000 cycles). Such high-rate capability and good cyclability can be associated with the low barrier for Na ion diffusion (0.24  0.44 eV) due to the existence of large tunnels.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit28"><sup><span class="sup_ref">28</span></sup></a> However, the higher electrode potential of 0.8 V <span class="italic">vs.</span> Na/Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> counter electrode has been found to be a major limiting point for anode applications of SIBs.</p>
<p class="otherpara">A remarkably low electrode potential of 0.3 V has been observed in step-layered sodium titanate Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (NTO), together with a high capacity of 178 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (theoretically 311 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>),<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit31"><sup><span class="sup_ref">3133</span></sup></a> being comparable with hard carbon. The crystalline structure of NTO is characterized by step layers of edge-sharing TiO<small><sub>6</sub></small> octahedra, which can accommodate 2 Na ions per formula unit, transforming into Na<small><sub>4</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> with a minor lattice expansion of 6%. In spite of the intrinsic benefit of its layered structure to ion diffusion, the rate capability of batteries is limited by the sluggish kinetics of Na ions and poor electronic conductivity.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit33"><sup><span class="sup_ref">33,34</span></sup></a> Three strategies have been developed to address this issue. Similar to other electrode materials, the first method is to use nanosize NTO made through elaborate synthesis routes, this shortens the transport path for ions and electrons.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit35"><sup><span class="sup_ref">3540</span></sup></a> However, a plateau voltage profile was often lost, and instead, a slope-like voltage profile was observed, indicating pseudocapacitance anode behaviour for sodium-ion capacitors (SICs).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit41"><sup><span class="sup_ref">41</span></sup></a> The second method is to introduce conductive layers such as carbon<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit42"><sup><span class="sup_ref">42,43</span></sup></a> and its derivatives<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit44"><sup><span class="sup_ref">44,45</span></sup></a> to enhance electronic conductivity. Doping or substituting Ti in NTO has been proved to be an effective third method for facilitating ionic and electronic transport.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit46"><sup><span class="sup_ref">4650</span></sup></a> In particular, Nb doping into NTO has shown an increase in unit cell volume and lower band gap, resulting in enhancement of rate capability to 89 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 5C and cyclability to 78.5%, after 500 cycles.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit48"><sup><span class="sup_ref">48</span></sup></a> Through first-principles calculations using density functional theory (DFT) framework, it was revealed that Ti/V exchange in NTO led to a lowered band gap and electrode potential with increased capacity.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit50"><sup><span class="sup_ref">50</span></sup></a> However, no comprehensive study of Nb- or V-doped NTO has yet been reported, but there are a few theoretical studies for NTO.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit15"><sup><span class="sup_ref">15,3234,50</span></sup></a></p>
<p class="otherpara">In this work, we perform systematic first-principles calculations on structural, electronic and electrochemical properties of Nb- and V-doped NTO compounds towards advanced anode materials for SIBs. To simulate the doping, we construct supercells for NTO  Nb-doped NTO (NTNO) and V-doped NTO (NTVO)  and apply the first-principles pseudopotential plane wave method as described in Section 2. The calculation results for the structural properties are provided in Subsection 3.1, and the energetic and electrode properties are given in Subsection 3.2. Subsections 3.3 and 3.4 explain the results for electronic and ionic conductivities, respectively. Finally, main conclusions are provided in Section 4.</p>

<h2 id="sect336"><span class="a_heading">2 Materials modeling and computational methods</span></h2>
<h3 id="sect339"><span class="b_heading">2.1 Modeling</span></h3>
<span>The NTO crystal are a monoclinic system with space group <span class="italic">P</span>2<small><sub>1</sub></small>/<span class="italic">m</span>.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit51"><sup><span class="sup_ref">51</span></sup></a> The unit cell with lattice constants of <span class="italic">a</span> = 9.118 , <span class="italic">b</span> = 3.795 , <span class="italic">c</span> = 8.563 , <span class="italic"></span> = <span class="italic"></span> = 90 and <span class="italic"></span> = 101.55 (ref. <a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit48">48</a>), contains 2 formula units (24 atoms). Titanium and oxygen ions form edge-sharing TiO<small><sub>6</sub></small> octahedra making a step layer  the step layers are connected with each other by a sharing vertex  and sodium ions are placed in the interlayer space with two different coordinations of 7 and 9. To investigate the doped structures and Na insertion/desertion, we built a supercell by doubling the unit cell in the crystallographic <span class="italic">b</span> direction (4 formula units, 48 atoms), as depicted in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1(a) and (b)</a>. The migration of Na ions was simulated using 2  2  1 supercells (8 formula units, 96 atoms) shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1(c)</a>.</span>
<br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig1"><a href="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-f1_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ra01755a-f1.tif" src="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-f1.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 1 </b> <span id="fig1"><span class="graphic_title">Crystalline structures of Nb- or V-doped Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small>. (a) Perspective view of supercell built by doubling the unit cell in the <span class="italic">b</span> direction, and (b) its top view. Brown-colored isosurface map of bond valence sum difference (BVS) with a value of 3, is shown to indicate the positions of the added Na ions and their diffusion path. (c) Perspective view of a 2  2  1 supercell for simulating Na ion diffusion.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<p class="otherpara">The doped structures can be realized by replacing Ti with transition metal (TM) M in the Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> crystal, where M represents one or more 4d and 3d TMs. Among the possible elements such as Nb, Mn (4d TMs) and V, Cr, Mo (3d TMs), Nb and V are preferred in this work. In the NTO unit cell, there are three different Ti positions. Therefore to fix the Ti/M (M = Nb, V) exchange position, we constructed the three different supercells where one of the 12 Ti ions was replaced by Nb or V, and performed structural optimization to select the one with the lowest total energy.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit50"><sup><span class="sup_ref">50,52</span></sup></a> The resultant compounds have the chemical formula Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti,<small><sub>2.75</sub></small>M,<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small>.</p>
<p class="otherpara">In Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small>, all the Ti ions have an oxidation state of +4 and some of them can be reduced to the +3 oxidation state upon insertion of Na ions for intercalation-type electrode application of SIBs. The preliminary positions of inserting Na ions can be identified by plotting the isosurface map of the bond valence sum difference (BVS), calculated by <a href="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-t1_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ra01755a-t1.tif" src="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-t1.gif"></a> where <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>i</sub></small>(<span class="bold"><span class="italic">r</span></span>) = |<span class="bold"><span class="italic">r</span></span>  <span class="italic"><span class="bold">R</span></span><small><sub>i</sub></small>|, where <span class="italic"><span class="bold">R</span></span><small><sub>i</sub></small> is the position vector of the i-th atom for the NaO bond.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit53"><sup><span class="sup_ref">53,54</span></sup></a> As shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1(a) and (b)</a>, there are 8 additional positions for Na ions in the doubled supercell, and we expect the final product Na<small><sub>4</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> with a specific capacity of 178 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> in accordance with experimental work.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit31"><sup><span class="sup_ref">31</span></sup></a> Eventually, one third of the total Ti ions retain the +4 state (Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small>2Ti<small><sup>3+</sup></small>). We note that Na<small><sub>5</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> with all Ti<small><sup>3+</sup></small> ions (311 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>) is not practically allowed due to the severe deviation of the cell.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit32"><sup><span class="sup_ref">32,50</span></sup></a> For the Nb- and V-doped NTOs, the same process is suggested with transformation M<small><sup>4+</sup></small>  M<small><sup>3+</sup></small>, based on experimental findings of a similar specific capacity to NTO.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit48"><sup><span class="sup_ref">48</span></sup></a> Considering that Nb and V have a +5 oxidation state as well, they might be in either M<small><sup>5+</sup></small> or M<small><sup>4+</sup></small> ionic states after doping into NTO. For the former circumstance, one Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small> ion could be transformed into a Ti<small><sup>3+</sup></small> ion for charge compensation, which nevertheless would not affect the Na insertion process suggested above.</p>

<h3 id="sect412"><span class="b_heading">2.2 Computational details</span></h3>
<span>All the DFT calculations were performed using the pseudopotential plan wave method as implemented in the Quantum ESPRESSO (version 6.5) package.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit55"><sup><span class="sup_ref">55</span></sup></a> The ultrasoft pseudopotentials provided in the GBRV library<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit56"><sup><span class="sup_ref">56</span></sup></a> were used to describe the electrostatic interaction between the ionic core and valence electrons with valence electron configurations of Na-2s<small><sup>2</sup></small>2p<small><sup>6</sup></small>3s<small><sup>1</sup></small>, Ti-3s<small><sup>2</sup></small>3p<small><sup>6</sup></small>3d<small><sup>2</sup></small>4s<small><sup>2</sup></small>, Nb-4s<small><sup>2</sup></small>4p<small><sup>6</sup></small>4d<small><sup>4</sup></small>5s<small><sup>1</sup></small>, V-3s<small><sup>2</sup></small>3p<small><sup>6</sup></small>3d<small><sup>3</sup></small>4s<small><sup>2</sup></small> and O-2s<small><sup>2</sup></small>2p<small><sup>4</sup></small>. The PerdewBurkeErnzerhof for solids (PBEsol) formulation within the generalized gradient approximation was adopted for the exchangecorrelation (XC) interaction.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit57"><sup><span class="sup_ref">57</span></sup></a> To take account of the localized 4d or 3d electrons of the TM elements, we used the DFT + <span class="italic">U</span> method,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit58"><sup><span class="sup_ref">58</span></sup></a> with the effective Hubbard parameter <span class="italic">U</span><small><sub>eff</sub></small> = 3.0 eV for Ti, Nb and V, consistent with previous DFT work.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit15"><sup><span class="sup_ref">15,50,59,60</span></sup></a> As the main computational parameters, the kinetic cutoff energies were set to 60 and 600 Ry for the wave function and electron density, respectively, and the <span class="italic">k</span>-point meshes for the Brillouin zone (BZ) integration were set to (2  2  2) for structural optimizations and (4  4  4) for density of states (DOS) calculations. The structural optimizations were finished when the atomic forces and the lattice pressure converged to 5  10<small><sup>4</sup></small> Ry bohr<small><sup>1</sup></small> and 0.05 kBar, respectively. These computational parameters guarantee the total energy accuracy of 5 meV per atom. Spin-polarization was considered in the DOS calculations.</span>
<p class="otherpara">To simulate the Na ion diffusion, we used the 2  2  1 supercells, which allows Na ion migration along the <span class="italic">a</span> and <span class="italic">b</span> directions, and only the  point for the BZ integration. The activation energies for the vacancy-mediated Na ion diffusions and the corresponding diffusion paths were determined by applying the climbing image nudged elastic band (NEB) method.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit61"><sup><span class="sup_ref">61</span></sup></a> The number of NEB image points was set to 7 along the migration path. During the NEB runs, the lattice constants of supercells were fixed, while all the atoms were relaxed until the forces converged to 0.01 eV <small><sup>1</sup></small>. The crystal structures were visualized using the VESTA code.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit62"><sup><span class="sup_ref">62</span></sup></a></p>


<h2 id="sect450"><span class="a_heading">3 Results and discussion</span></h2>
<h3 id="sect453"><span class="b_heading">3.1 Structural properties</span></h3>
<span>Firstly, the lattice parameters of the NTO unit cell with 2 formula units (24 atoms) were determined by performing structural optimization using the PBEsol functional. The optimized lattice constants are <span class="italic">a</span> = 9.089 , <span class="italic">b</span> = 3.800 , <span class="italic">c</span> = 8.532  and <span class="italic"></span> = 101.82, which are in good agreement with the experimental values of <span class="italic">a</span> = 9.118 , <span class="italic">b</span> = 3.795 , <span class="italic">c</span> = 8.563  and <span class="italic"></span> = 101.55.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit48"><sup><span class="sup_ref">48</span></sup></a> The relative errors are less than 0.6%, indicating that our selections for computation, including the pseudopotentials, XC functional and <span class="italic">U</span><small><sub>eff</sub></small> values, can provide reliable results for electrochemical and electronic properties.</span>
<p class="otherpara">With the same computational settings, the structural optimization of the doubled supercells with 4 formula units (48 atoms) for NTO, NTNO and NTVO were then performed. <a title="Select to navigate to table" href="#tab1">Table 1</a> lists the optimized lattice constants and cell volumes in comparison with the available experimental data. As mentioned above, the configuration with the lowest total energy was selected among the three different configurations for the doped NTO supercells. In <a title="Select to navigate to table" href="#tab1">Table 1</a>, we list the experimental lattice constants for Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti,<small><sub>2.97</sub></small>Nb,<small><sub>0.03</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small>,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit48"><sup><span class="sup_ref">48</span></sup></a> which has a significantly lower concentration of doping Nb ions compared with our case of Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti,<small><sub>2.75</sub></small>Nb,<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small>. It was found that the cell volume was slightly expanded by Nb doping with a relative volume expansion rate of 0.91%, estimated by <span class="italic">r</span><small><sub>vol</sub></small> = (<span class="italic">V</span><small><sub>NTNO</sub></small>  <span class="italic">V</span><small><sub>NTO</sub></small>)/<span class="italic">V</span><small><sub>NTO</sub></small>  100%, in accordance with the experiment. This value of <span class="italic">r</span><small><sub>vol</sub></small> is larger than the value of 0.19% estimated from experiments, due to the higher concentration of doping Nb ions in this work. The volume expansion by Nb doping is attributed to larger ionic radius of Nb<small><sup>4+</sup></small> (0.68 ) or Nb<small><sup>5+</sup></small> (0.64 ) and Ti<small><sup>3+</sup></small> (0.67 ) than that of Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small> (0.605 ). In contrast, V doping was found to shrink the cell volume with a <span class="italic">r</span><small><sub>vol</sub></small> value of 0.42% because of smaller ionic radii of the V<small><sup>4+</sup></small> (0.58 ) and V<small><sup>5+</sup></small> (0.54 ) ions.</p>

<hr class="hrule"><br>
<p class="otherpara">In the next step, we identified the intermediate phases formed by inserting additional Na ions into the host compounds NTO, NTNO and NTVO, for suitability in the charge/discharge process in SIBs. As expected from BVS analysis, the content of additional Na ions could be allowed to vary between 0 and 2, forming intermediate phases of Na<small><sub>2+<span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>TO, with insignificant structural variation. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2</a> shows the variation tendencies of lattice constants and volumes of the doubled supercells for Na<small><sub>2+<span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>TO, Na<small><sub>2+<span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>TNO and Na<small><sub>2+<span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>TVO, with increasing Na content <span class="italic">x</span> from 0 to 2 with an interval of 0.25. It should be noted that there exists numerous configurations for Na insertion at each value of Na content <span class="italic">x</span>, and the lowest energy configuration was picked out with performing structural optimization (see Fig. S1S3 for final configurations).<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a></p>
<br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig2"><a href="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-f2_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ra01755a-f2.tif" src="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-f2.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 2 </b> <span id="fig2"><span class="graphic_title">Variation tendency of (a) lattice constants (<span class="italic">a</span>, <span class="italic">b</span> and <span class="italic">c</span>), (b) supercell volume, and (c) volume expansion rate in the doubled supercells for Na<small><sub>2+<span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (NTO), Na<small><sub>2+<span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ti,<small><sub>2.75</sub></small>Nb,<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (NTNO) and Na<small><sub>2+<span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ti,<small><sub>2.75</sub></small>V,<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (NTVO), with increasing Na content <span class="italic">x</span> from 0 to 2.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<p class="otherpara">For all three compounds, the lattice constants <span class="italic">a</span> and <span class="italic">b</span> were found to increase gradually with increasing Na content <span class="italic">x</span>, whereas the lattice constant <span class="italic">c</span>, <span class="italic">i.e.</span>, the interlayer distance, was found to decrease gradually until <span class="italic">x</span> = 1.5 and then it decreased rapidly, as shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2(a)</a>. Of course, some wavy features were observed. This indicates that the interaction between the step layers can be enhanced <span class="italic">via</span> the attractive NaO ionic bonding by insertion of additional Na ions into the interlayer space, while the repulsion between Na ions and TM ions is dominant in the lateral directions. As can be seen in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2(b)</a>, the supercell volumes were found to overall increase with increasing Na content <span class="italic">x</span> from 0 to 1.5, then the volumes decrease abruptly at <span class="italic">x</span> = 1.75 and again increase at <span class="italic">x</span> = 2 for NTO, NTNO and NTVO. The abrupt decrease of volume at <span class="italic">x</span> = 1.75 is associated with the rapid decrease of the interlayer distance due to the enhancement of layerlayer interactions. Across the whole range of Na content, the volumes of Nb-doped NTO supercells are larger while the volumes of V-doped NTO supercells are smaller, than those of NTO supercells, an effect ascribed to the ionic radii of TM ions as discussed previously. To check the cycling stability during charge/discharge processes, we evaluated the relative volume expansion rate <span class="italic">r</span><small><sub>vol</sub></small> with respect to the volumes of the host compounds at <span class="italic">x</span> = 0 as shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2(c)</a>. The variation tendencies are similar to those of the cell volumes. Most importantly, the maximal values of <span class="italic">r</span><small><sub>vol</sub></small> found at <span class="italic">x</span> = 1.5 are below 3%, being much smaller than other intercalation-type electrode materials (usually 5  6%) as well as alloy-type electrode materials. This indicates that the NTO-related compounds under study can exhibit superior cycling stabilities.</p>

<h3 id="sect636"><span class="b_heading">3.2 Energetics and electrode potential</span></h3>
<span>The formability of the intermediate phases can be assessed by calculating their formation energies from the hosts and Na bulk in the body-centered cubic (bcc) phase as follows,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit63"><sup><span class="sup_ref">63</span></sup></a><table><tbody><tr><td class="leftEqn">&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td class="eqn"><span id="eqn1">
<a href="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-t2_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ra01755a-t2.tif" src="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-t2.gif"></a></span></td><td class="rightEqn">(1)</td></tr></tbody></table>where <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>Na(bulk)</sub></small> is the total energy of the relevant compound and M stands for Ti, Ti,<small><sub>2.75/3</sub></small>Nb,<small><sub>0.25/3</sub></small> and Ti,<small><sub>2.75/3</sub></small>V,<small><sub>0.25/3</sub></small>. The negative value of <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>f</sub></small> indicates spontaneous formation of the intermediate phase from the host and Na bulk, while the positive value is indicative of their endothermic formation, <span class="italic">i.e.</span>, non-spontaneous formation. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3(a)</a> displays the calculated formation energy curves as a function of Na content <span class="italic">x</span>, ranging from 0.25 to 2. It was found that the formation energies varied between 0.9 eV and 0.3 eV, indicating certain formations of the intermediate phases. With increasing Na content <span class="italic">x</span>, the <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>f</sub></small> values were shown to decrease gradually until <span class="italic">x</span> = 1.5 and then increase slightly in magnitude, implying the weakening of formability, which is in accordance with the variation of the cell volumes. In the meantime, the formability could be weakened going from NTO to V-doped and to Nb-doped NTO compounds since the <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>f</sub></small> values were decreased in magnitude across the whole Na content range.</span>
<br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig3"><a href="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-f3_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ra01755a-f3.tif" src="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-f3.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 3 </b> <span id="fig3"><span class="graphic_title">(a) Formation energy per Na atom of the Na-ion insertion intermediate phases resulting in Na<small><sub>2+<span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small>, Na<small><sub>2+<span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ti,<small><sub>2.75</sub></small>Nb,<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> and Na<small><sub>2+<span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>Ti,<small><sub>2.75</sub></small>V,<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> with Na content <span class="italic">x</span> ranging from 0.25 to 2, estimated from the total energies of hosts (<span class="italic">x</span> = 0) and bcc phase Na bulk, and (b) binding energy per Na atom between the host and inserted Na atom, estimated from the total energies of the hosts and isolated Na atom.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<p class="otherpara">To check the binding strength between the host and inserted Na ions, the binding energy <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>b</sub></small> per Na atom was calculated using the following equation,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit63"><sup><span class="sup_ref">63</span></sup></a></p><table><tbody><tr><td class="leftEqn">&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td class="eqn"><span id="eqn2">
<a href="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-t3_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ra01755a-t3.tif" src="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-t3.gif"></a></span></td><td class="rightEqn">(2)</td></tr></tbody></table>where <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>Na(atom)</sub></small> is the total energy of the isolated Na atom calculated using the cubic supercell with a lattice constant of 15  and only the  point in the first BZ. As shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3(b)</a>, the binding energies could vary between 2.6 eV and 2.0 eV with the same variation tendencies as the formation energies: the binding strength was found to gradually decrease with increasing Na content, with the highest to lowest going from NTO to NTVO and to NTNO.<p></p>
<p class="otherpara">We also estimated the relative stability of the intermediate phases with respect to the starting (<span class="italic">x</span> = 0) and ending (<span class="italic">x</span> = 2) compounds for additional Na insertion. To this end, the formation enthalpies were calculated using the following equation,<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit64"><sup><span class="sup_ref">64,65</span></sup></a></p><table><tbody><tr><td class="leftEqn">&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td class="eqn"><span id="eqn3">
<a href="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-t4_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ra01755a-t4.tif" src="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-t4.gif"></a></span></td><td class="rightEqn">(3)</td></tr></tbody></table>where Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>M<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> and Na<small><sub>4</sub></small>M<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> are the initial and final compounds for Na insertion. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4(a)</a> shows the calculated convex hull curves for the formation enthalpies of NTO, NTNO and NTVO as functions of Na content <span class="italic">x</span> ranging between 0 and 2. For the three kinds of compounds, the intermediate phases with <span class="italic">x</span> = 0.25, 0.5, 0.75 and 1.0 were found to be stable because their formation enthalpy values were laid on the convex hull. However, other phases with <span class="italic">x</span> = 1.25, 1.5 and 1.75 were found to be unstable with respect to the two end compounds, <span class="italic">i.e.</span>, these phases could not be formed in reality during the charge/discharge process. The intermediate phase with the lowest formation enthalpy was observed at <span class="italic">x</span> = 0.75 for NTO but at <span class="italic">x</span> = 1 for the NTNO and NTVO compounds. Moreover, the formation enthalpies of NTNO and NTVO were overall lower compared with NTO due to the weakening of the interactions between cations and anions by Nb or V doping. Also, the Nb-doped NTNO phases exhibited slightly lower formation energies than the V-doped NTVO phases, indicating that the former phases can be formed more easily than the latter ones. This can be associated with the fact that the interaction strength between the Nb<small><sup>5+,4+</sup></small> cations and O<small><sup>2</sup></small> anions is higher than that between the V<small><sup>5+,4+</sup></small> cations and O<small><sup>2</sup></small>, leading to the enhanced relative stability of the NTNO intermediate phases compared with the NTVO ones.<p></p>
<br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig4"><a href="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-f4_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ra01755a-f4.tif" src="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-f4.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 4 </b> <span id="fig4"><span class="graphic_title">(a) Convex hull plot for formation enthalpies of the intermediate phases from the initial (<span class="italic">x</span> = 0) and final compounds (<span class="italic">x</span> = 2) for additional Na insertion in NTO, NTNO and NTVO as a function of Na content <span class="italic">x</span>. (b) Step-like electrode potential as a function of specific capacity calculated using the formation enthalpies of the stable phases identified by the convex hull.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<p class="otherpara">With these stable intermediate phases identified by the convex hull, we calculated the step-like electrode potential with respect to the Na/Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> counter electrode. The electrode potential between the adjacent phases at <span class="italic">x</span><small><sub>i</sub></small> and <span class="italic">x</span><small><sub>j</sub></small> could be calculated using the total energies of the relevant phases as follows,<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit50"><sup><span class="sup_ref">50,64,66</span></sup></a></p><table><tbody><tr><td class="leftEqn">&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td class="eqn"><span id="eqn4">
<a href="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-t5_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ra01755a-t5.tif" src="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-t5.gif"></a></span></td><td class="rightEqn">(4)</td></tr></tbody></table>where <span class="italic">e</span> is the elementary charge. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4(b)</a> shows the determined step-like electrode potentials for NTO, NTNO and NTVO as functions of specific capacity, which varies between 0 to 177.6, 171.2 and 177.2 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, respectively. Such reduction of specific capacity with Nb or V doping is due to their heavier atomic weights compared to Ti. It was found that the electrode potential in the plateau region became 0.05 V higher by Nb doping and 0.11 V higher by V doping compared with NTO. The calculated electrode potential steps for NTO and NTNO were in reasonable agreement with the experimentally observed electrode potential profiles.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit48"><sup><span class="sup_ref">48</span></sup></a> It is worth noting that the discharge curves look like having long plateau portions, indicating that the materials under study could be used as electrode active materials in SIBs rather than as capacitor electrode materials in SICs. It turned out from our calculations, that the energy density of SIBs employing NTO as the anode material could be slightly lowered by Nb or V doping due to the reduction of specific capacity and the rise in electrode potential.<p></p>

<h3 id="sect732"><span class="b_heading">3.3 Electronic properties</span></h3>
<span>From previous theoretical and experimental works,<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit15"><sup><span class="sup_ref">15,33</span></sup></a> it was found that NTO itself has a wide band gap of 3.53.7 eV and therefore it is an electrically insulating compound. This is unfavorable for electron transfer during the charge/discharge process, and thus a conductive agent such as carbon black should be added to the electrode. When doping with Nb or V, the band gap can be expected to decrease due to the increased valence electron density, thereby improving the electron conductivity. To check the electronic conduction improvement, we calculated the electronic density of states (DOS) in the compounds. The initial and final compounds Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> and Na<small><sub>4</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small>, denoted as NTO-2 and NTO-4, and their Nb- or V-doped counterparts were selected for electronic structure calculations. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5</a> shows the atom-resolved partial DOS of these compounds, calculated using the PBEsol XC functional and DFT + <span class="italic">U</span> method.</span>
<br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig5"><a href="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-f5_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ra01755a-f5.tif" src="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-f5.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 5 </b> <span id="fig5"><span class="graphic_title">Atomic resolved partial density of states (DOS) in Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (NTO-2), Na<small><sub>4</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (NTO-4), Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti,<small><sub>2.75</sub></small>Nb,<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (NTNO-2), Na<small><sub>4</sub></small>Ti,<small><sub>2.75</sub></small>Nb,<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (NTNO-4), Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti,<small><sub>2.75</sub></small>V,<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (NTVO-2) and Na<small><sub>4</sub></small>Ti,<small><sub>2.75</sub></small>V,<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (NTVO-4), calculated with the PBEsol functional and DFT + <span class="italic">U</span> method. Fermi level (<span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>F</sub></small>) indicated by the vertical dashed line is set to zero.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<p class="otherpara">In our calculations, the band gap of NTO-2 was determined to be 3.37 eV, which is very close to the experimental value. The final compound NTO-4 formed by inserting additional Na ions, showed a lower band gap of 2.78 eV, possibly due to the increased density of conduction band states originating from additional Na ions. When doping with Nb, the band gaps were found to be slightly reduced to lower than 0.10.2 eV for both NTNO-2 (3.20 eV) and NTNO-4 (2.68 eV) with almost no preservation of the DOS shape compared with the undoped counterparts. From the orbital-resolved partial DOS analysis, it was found that the conduction band states were dominated by Ti 3d and Nb 4d equally (see Fig. S4 and S5<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). Meanwhile, the V-doped compounds, NTVO-2 and NTVO-4, exhibited much lower band gaps of 2.40 and 1.66 eV, respectively, with the characteristic peaks originating from V 3d near the conduction band minimum (CBM) (see also Fig. S6 and S7<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). As shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6</a>, for the integrated local density of states, the valence band states close to the valence band maximum (VBM) were composed of O s states with minor contribution from the TM d states, while the conduction band states close to CBM were attributed to the TM d states with minor contribution of the O p states (see Fig. S8<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). Based on the calculation results, it can be concluded that the electron conductivity can surely be improved by Nb or V doping.</p>
<br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig6"><a href="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-f6_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ra01755a-f6.tif" src="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-f6.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 6 </b> <span id="fig6"><span class="graphic_title">Isosurface plot for integrated local density of states with energies from the valence band maximum (VBM) to VBM 1 eV (left panel), and from conduction band minimum (CBM) to CBM +1 eV (right panel) in (a) Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (NTO-2), (b) Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti,<small><sub>2.75</sub></small>Nb,<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (NTNO-2) and (c) Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti,<small><sub>2.75</sub></small>V,<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (NTVO-2).</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<p class="otherpara">To get an understanding of electron transfer upon Na ion insertion during the charge/discharge process, we evaluated the Lwdin charges of each atom, as listed in Table S1.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> In NTO-2, the average charges were found to be 0.73, 1.5 and 0.8 for Na, Ti and O, respectively. Upon insertion of 8 Na ions, the average charge of Na ion was slightly reduced to 0.7, while oxygen showed a value increased by 0.9. Interestingly, 4 Ti ions kept the charge as 1.5 but 8 Ti ions exhibited the reduced value of 1.2, confirming the partial reduction of Ti ions upon Na insertion for the discharge process, 3Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small>  Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small>2Ti<small><sup>3+</sup></small>. In the case of NTNO-2, one Ti ion close to Nb had a smaller charge of 1.3 compared to the average value 1.5 in the other Ti ions, implying the reduction of the Ti ion upon Ti/Nb exchange for the sake of charge compensation, <span class="italic">i.e.</span>, 2Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small>  Nb<small><sup>5+</sup></small>Ti<small><sup>3+</sup></small>. When inserting Na ions into NTNO-2, 4 Ti ions also maintained the charge state as 1.5, while 7 Ti ions and Nb ion exhibited a reduction, indicating the partial reduction during the discharge process, 2.5Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small>0.25Ti<small><sup>3+</sup></small>0.25Nb<small><sup>5+</sup></small>  Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small>1.75Ti<small><sup>3+</sup></small>0.25Nb<small><sup>4+</sup></small>. On the contrary, none of the 11 Ti ions had a change in charge state from 1.5 upon Ti/V exchange, thereby indicating that the V ion was in the V<small><sup>4+</sup></small> state. In NTVO-4, 4 Ti ions had an atomic charge of 1.5 while the remaining Ti ions and the V ion showed a reduction, thereby indicating the reduction of TM ions like 2.75Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small>0.25V<small><sup>4+</sup></small>  Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small>1.75Ti<small><sup>3+</sup></small>0.25V<small><sup>3+</sup></small>.</p>

<h3 id="sect811"><span class="b_heading">3.4 Ion conductivity</span></h3>
<span>The Na ion conductivity determines the rate capability and cycling life of SIBs, together with the relative volume expansion rate. Therefore, we investigated the Na ion diffusion, which was expected to occur naturally within the interlayer space and according to the vacancy-mediated mechanism like in most insertion-type layered electrode materials. The 2  2  1 supercells were used to get more reasonable insight into the Na ion conduction. As shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7(a) and (b)</a>, we suggested 4 different pathways to consider all the possible ways for the Na ion migration within the interlayer space; (1) pathway of ascending the step in the (100) direction (Path 1), pathway of horizontal moving on the step in the (010) direction (Path 2), pathway of diagonal moving on the step in the (110) direction (Path 3 and Path 4). We estimated the activation energies for Na ion diffusion along these pathways by applying the NEB method. It should be noted that the Na ion diffusion across the layer was not allowed, undoubtedly due to obstacles formed by the MO<small><sub>6</sub></small> octahedra and thus much higher activation energy.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit33"><sup><span class="sup_ref">33</span></sup></a></span>
<br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig7"><a href="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-f7_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ra01755a-f7.tif" src="/image/article/2023/RA/d3ra01755a/d3ra01755a-f7.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 7 </b> <span id="fig7"><span class="graphic_title">Pathways of Na ion migration within the interlayer space in (a) top and (b) side view, showing 4 different pathways, and (c) calculated energy profiles for Na ion migration along the 4 different pathways according to the vacancy-mediated mechanism in Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>M<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (M = Ti, Ti<small><sub>0.96</sub></small>Nb<small><sub>0.04</sub></small>, Ti<small><sub>0.96</sub></small>V<small><sub>0.04</sub></small>) compounds.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<p class="otherpara"><a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7(c)</a> displays the calculated energy profiles for Na ion migration along these suggested pathways. Along Path 1, the activation energies were determined to be 0.75, 0.77 and 0.79 eV for NTO, NTNO and NTVO, respectively. These are relatively high compared with those along other pathways, indicating that the Na migration ascending the step could not occur in reality. The horizontal Na ion migration along the (010) direction (Path 2) produced the energy difference curves with a two-peaks feature, for which the activation energies were calculated to be 0.30, 0.25 and 0.22 eV for NTO, NTVO and NTNO, respectively. For the case of NTO, although slightly underestimated, the calculated value was in good agreement with the experimental value of 0.39 eV.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit67"><sup><span class="sup_ref">67</span></sup></a> The reduction of activation energy by Nb or V doping, indicating the improvement of Na ion conductivity, could be attributed to the enhancement of cationcation repulsion. Meanwhile, along Path 3 in the diagonal direction, the activation energy was found to be 0.47 eV for NTO and slightly reduced by Nb or V doping. Also, the activation energy along Path 4 was reduced from 0.22 eV for NTO to 0.21 eV by V doping and to 0.19 eV by Nb doping. To sum up, the Na ion conductivity on the step layer can be enhanced by V doping and furthermore by Nb doping. Such enhancement of Na ion conductivity by Nb or V doping can be ascribed to the enhancement of repulsion between the Na cation and TM cations, occurring the charge state change of 2Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small>  Nb<small><sup>5+</sup></small>Ti<small><sup>3+</sup></small> or V<small><sup>4+</sup></small>Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small>.</p>
<p class="otherpara">Finally we estimated the diffusion coefficients using the calculated activation energies <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small> and the Arrhenius equation, <span class="italic">D</span> = <span class="italic">a</span><small><sup>2</sup></small><span class="italic"></span><img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_2009.gif" alt="[thin space (1/6-em)]">exp(<span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>a</sub></small>/<span class="italic">k</span><small><sub>B</sub></small><span class="italic">T</span>) with <span class="italic">a</span>  4 , <span class="italic"></span>  10<small><sup>11</sup></small> Hz and <span class="italic">k</span><small><sub>B</sub></small><span class="italic">T</span> = 0.026 eV at room temperature.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit33"><sup><span class="sup_ref">33</span></sup></a> The activation energies for Na ion migration only, along Path 2 were considered here. <a title="Select to navigate to table" href="#tab2">Table 2</a> presents the calculated diffusion coefficients of NTO, NTNO and NTVO, together with other electrochemical properties determined in this work. They exhibited relatively high diffusion coefficients of 1.54  10<small><sup>9</sup></small>, 3.09  10<small><sup>8</sup></small> and 9.91  10<small><sup>9</sup></small> cm<small><sup>2</sup></small> s<small><sup>1</sup></small> along the horizontal path, confirming the enhancement of Na ion diffusibility by Nb or V doping. As presented in <a title="Select to navigate to table" href="#tab2">Table 2</a>, the relative volume expansion rate, specific capacity and electrode potential, could be weakened but the electronic and ionic conductivities could be enhanced by Nb or V doping.</p>

<div class="table_caption"><b>Table 2</b> <span id="tab2">Material properties of Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (NTO), Nb-doped NTO (NTNO) and V-doped NTO (NTVO), calculated in this work</span>
		</div>

<hr class="hrule"><br>


<h2 id="sect913"><span class="a_heading">4 Conclusions</span></h2>
<span>In this work, we have investigated the effect of Nb or V doping into sodium titanate Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small>, on the electrode performance using first-principles calculations, aiming to find advanced anode materials for sodium-ion batteries. We made materials models for Nb- or V-doped NTO using the doubled supercells, forming Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti,<small><sub>2.75</sub></small>M,<small><sub>0.25</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> (M = Nb, V), to investigate the structural, electrochemical and electronic properties, and the 2  2  1 supercells for studying the Na ion diffusion. From structural optimization, it was found that the Nb doping increased the supercell volume with the relative volume expansion rate <span class="italic">r</span><small><sub>vol</sub></small> of 0.9% due to the larger ionic radius of the Nb ion, whereas the V doping shrank the cell volume with the <span class="italic">r</span><small><sub>vol</sub></small> value of 0.4% because of the smaller ionic radius of the V ion. Through BVS analysis, the final sodiation compound was fixed as Na<small><sub>4</sub></small>M<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small> and the positions for inserting Na ions into the interlayer space were identified. We performed structural optimizations of the intermediate phases Na<small><sub>2+<span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>M<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small>, with increasing Na content <span class="italic">x</span> from 0 to 2, finding that the intermediate phases could be formed exothermically from the NTO and Na bulk as the negative formation energies and maximum <span class="italic">r</span><small><sub>vol</sub></small> values could be slightly increased by Nb or V doping, but remained lower than 3%. The formation enthalpies of the intermediate phases were calculated with respect to the initial (NTO-2) and final (NTO-4) compounds, to plot the convex hull and electrode potential curves, revealing that the electrode potential could be slightly raised and the specific capacity could be reduced by Nb or V doping. Through DOS analysis, it was found that the band gap of 3.37 eV in NTO was reduced to 3.20 eV in NTNO-2 and to 2.40 eV in NTVO-2, which was ascribed to the 4d state of Nb and 3d state of V, indicating the improvement of electronic conductivity by doping. The redox couples during sodiation were identified through the analysis of the Lwdin charge of the atoms. Finally, we calculated the activation energies for the vacancy-mediated Na ion migration and found significant improvement of Na ion conductivity from Nb or V doping.</span>

<h2 id="sect938"><span class="a_heading">Author contributions</span></h2>
<span>Suk-Gyong Hwang performed the calculations and drafted the first manuscript. Chung-Hyok Kim performed the post-processing of calculation results. Song-Hyok Choe and Kum-Chol Ri assisted with the DFT calculations and contributed to useful discussions. Chol-Jun Yu developed the original project and supervised the work. All authors reviewed the manuscript.</span>
